void deleterecord()
{
    struct person p;
    FILE *f,*ft;
	int flag;
	char name[100];
	f=fopen("project","rb");
	if(f==NULL)
		{

			printf("CONTACT'S DATA NOT ADDED YET.");

		}
	else
	{
		ft=fopen("temp","wb+");
		if(ft==NULL)

            printf("file opaning error");
		else

        {


		printf("Enter CONTACT'S NAME:");
		got(name);

		fflush(stdin);
		while(fread(&p,sizeof(p),1,f)==1)
		{
			if(strcmp(p.name,name)!=0)
				fwrite(&p,sizeof(p),1,ft);
			if(strcmp(p.name,name)==0)
                flag=1;
		}
	fclose(f);
	fclose(ft);
	if(flag!=1)
	{
		printf("NO CONACT'S RECORD TO DELETE.");
		remove("temp.txt");
	}
		else
		{
			remove("project");
			rename("temp.txt","project");
			printf("RECORD DELETED SUCCESSFULLY.");

		}
	}
}
 printf("\n Enter any key");

	 getch();
    system("cls");
menu();
}

void got(char *name)
{

   int i=0,j;
    char c,ch;
    do
    {
        c=getch();
                if(c!=8&&c!=13)
                {
                    *(name+i)=c;
                        putch(c);
                        i++;
                }
                if(c==8)
                {
                    if(i>0)
                    {
                        i--;
                    }
                   // printf("h");
                    system("cls");
                    for(j=0;j<i;j++)
                    {
                        ch=*(name+j);
                        putch(ch);

                    }

                }
    }while(c!=13);
      *(name+i)='\0';
}
[05/04/23, 10:18:23â€¯AM] Ragesh: Monitoring and management of crop growth
[05/04/23, 10:18:24â€¯AM] Ragesh: import time
import random

# Define the crops being grown and their ideal growing conditions
crops = {
    "tomatoes": {
        "ideal_temperature": 21,
        "ideal_humidity": 60,
        "ideal_light": 1000
    },
    "lettuce": {
        "ideal_temperature": 18,
        "ideal_humidity": 80,
        "ideal_light": 800
    }
}

# Define the sensors and equipment being used
temperature_sensor = Sensor("Temperature")
humidity_sensor = Sensor("Humidity")
light_sensor = Sensor("Light")
irrigation_system = IrrigationSystem()

# Define a function to read the sensor data and update the crop conditions
def update_crop_conditions():
    current_temperature = temperature_sensor.read()
    current_humidity = humidity_sensor.read()
    current_light = light_sensor.read()
    for crop in crops:
        if current_temperature < crops[crop]["ideal_temperature"]:
            irrigation_system.turn_on()
        if current_humidity < crops[crop]["ideal_humidity"]:
            irrigation_system.turn_on()
        if current_light < crops[crop]["ideal_light"]:
            irrigation_system.turn_on()

# Define a function to simulate sensor readings
def simulate_sensor_readings():
    temperature_sensor.set_value(random.randint(10, 30))
    humidity_sensor.set_value(random.randint(40, 90))
    light_sensor.set_value(random.randint(500, 1500))

# Run the monitoring and management system
while True:
    simulate_sensor_readings()
    update_crop_conditions()
    time.sleep(60)

import time    
    
board = [' ',' ',' ',' ',' ',' ',' ',' ',' ',' ']    
player = 1    
   
########win Flags##########    
Win = 1    
Draw = -1    
Running = 0    
Stop = 1    
###########################    
Game = Running    
Mark = 'X'    
   
#This Function Draws Game Board    
def DrawBoard():    
    print(" %c | %c | %c " % (board[1],board[2],board[3]))    
    print("___|___|___")    
    print(" %c | %c | %c " % (board[4],board[5],board[6]))    
    print("___|___|___")    
    print(" %c | %c | %c " % (board[7],board[8],board[9]))    
    print("   |   |   ")    
   
#This Function Checks position is empty or not    
def CheckPosition(x):    
    if(board[x] == ' '):    
        return True    
    else:    
        return False    
   
#This Function Checks player has won or not    
def CheckWin():    
    global Game    
    #Horizontal winning condition    
    if(board[1] == board[2] and board[2] == board[3] and board[1] != ' '):    
        Game = Win    
    elif(board[4] == board[5] and board[5] == board[6] and board[4] != ' '):    
        Game = Win    
    elif(board[7] == board[8] and board[8] == board[9] and board[7] != ' '):    
        Game = Win    
    #Vertical Winning Condition    
    elif(board[1] == board[4] and board[4] == board[7] and board[1] != ' '):    
        Game = Win    
    elif(board[2] == board[5] and board[5] == board[8] and board[2] != ' '):    
        Game = Win    
    elif(board[3] == board[6] and board[6] == board[9] and board[3] != ' '):    
        Game=Win    
    #Diagonal Winning Condition    
    elif(board[1] == board[5] and board[5] == board[9] and board[5] != ' '):    
        Game = Win    
    elif(board[3] == board[5] and board[5] == board[7] and board[5] != ' '):    
        Game=Win    
    #Match Tie or Draw Condition    
    elif(board[1]!=' ' and board[2]!=' ' and board[3]!=' ' and board[4]!=' ' and board[5]!=' ' and board[6]!=' ' and board[7]!=' ' and board[8]!=' ' and board[9]!=' '):    
        Game=Draw    
    else:            
        Game=Running    
    
print("Tic-Tac-Toe Game Designed By Sourabh Somani")    
print("Player 1 [X] --- Player 2 [O]\n")    
print()    
print()    
print("Please Wait...")    
time.sleep(3)    
while(Game == Running):    
    os.system('cls')    
    DrawBoard()    
    if(player % 2 != 0):    
        print("Player 1's chance")    
        Mark = 'X'    
    else:    
        print("Player 2's chance")    
        Mark = 'O'    
    choice = int(input("Enter the position between [1-9] where you want to mark : "))    
    if(CheckPosition(choice)):    
        board[choice] = Mark    
        player+=1    
        CheckWin()    
    
os.system('cls')    
DrawBoard()    
if(Game==Draw):    
    print("Game Draw")    
elif(Game==Win):    
    player-=1    
    if(player%2!=0):    
        print("Player 1 Won")    
    else:    
        print("Player 2 Won")

[11/04/23, 6:45:36â€¯PM] Prem: ...
[11/04/23, 10:35:15â€¯PM] Yash: 2 mark

1. Describe common Association pattern
A .describe the association between two variables by interpreting a scatterplot, to interpret a correlation coefficient, and to understand the limitations of correlation coefficients.

2.write about DDL and DML
Ans: DDL stands for Data Definition Language, which defines the structure or schema of the database. DML, or the Data Manipulation Language, helps us deal with managing and manipulating data in the database. DCL, or the Data Control Language, helps us deal with controls, rights, and permission in the database system.

3. List out the types of visibility
Ans: The three visibility modes are private, protected and public.

4.mention any four rules of object oriented database system?
Ans:These are Encapsulation, Data Abstraction, Polymorphism and Inheritance. These are also called as four pillars of Object Oriented Programming.

5. Define OCL?
Ans:Object Constraint Language
The Object Constraint Language (OCL) is a declarative language describing rules applying to Unified Modeling Language (UML) models developed at IBM and is now part of the UML standard.

6. write about properties of relationship

7.define DBMS
A database management system (or DBMS) is essentially nothing more than a computerized data-keeping system. Users of the system are given facilities to perform several kinds of operations on such a system for either manipulation of the data in the database or the management of the database structure itself.

8.what is schema.
A database schema defines how data is organized within a relational database; this is inclusive of logical constraints such as, table names, fields, data types, and the relationships between these entities.

9.why analysis is a difficult activity 

10. What is axioms
Armstrong's Axiom is a mathematical notation used to find the functional dependencies in a database. Conceived by William W. Armstrong, it is a list of axioms or inference rules that can be implemented on any relational database. It is denoted by the symbol F+.

[13/04/23, 5:06:03â€¯AM] Praveen A: ```UNIT 3
Part - A
1. Memory-mapped I/O and I/O-mapped I/O are two methods used in microprocessors to communicate with I/O devices. Memory-mapped I/O uses the same address space as the memory for both memory and I/O devices. In contrast, I/O-mapped I/O uses a separate address space for I/O devices. In memory-mapped I/O, the processor communicates with I/O devices using load and store instructions, while in I/O-mapped I/O, the processor communicates with I/O devices using specific input and output instructions.

2. The hardware interrupts of 8085 are:
- INTR (Interrupt Request)
- RST 7.5 (Restart 7.5)
- RST 6.5 (Restart 6.5)
- RST 5.5 (Restart 5.5)
- TRAP

The software interrupts of 8085 are:
- RST 0 (Restart 0)
- RST 1 (Restart 1)
- RST 2 (Restart 2)
- RST 3 (Restart 3)
- RST 4 (Restart 4)

3. Masking is the process of blocking or allowing certain interrupts in a microprocessor. It is required to prioritize the interrupts and avoid conflicts. When an interrupt occurs, the microprocessor suspends its current execution and serves the interrupt. However, if multiple interrupts occur simultaneously, the microprocessor must decide which one to serve first. By masking certain interrupts, the microprocessor can prioritize and handle them in a specific order.

4. The HOLD signal is used to request the microprocessor to halt its current execution and enter a HOLD state. In this state, the microprocessor relinquishes control of the system bus and waits for an external device to take control. The HOLD signal is typically used by slower devices that need to access the system bus temporarily, such as an I/O device that needs to transfer data.

5. DI (Disable Interrupts) and EI (Enable Interrupts) are instructions used in microprocessors to control the interrupt system. The DI instruction disables the interrupts, while the EI instruction enables them. These instructions are used to prevent interrupts from occurring during critical sections of code or to re-enable interrupts after they have been masked.

Unit-4
Part-A
1. The 8086 microcontroller can operate in two modes: minimum mode and maximum mode.

2. The data size of the 8086 microcontroller is 16 bits, while the address size is 20 bits.

3. The segment registers of 8086 are:
- Code Segment (CS)
- Data Segment (DS)
- Stack Segment (SS)
- Extra Segment (ES)

4. The various flags of 8086 are:
- Carry flag (CF)
- Parity flag (PF)
- Auxiliary Carry flag (AF)
- Zero flag (ZF)
- Sign flag (SF)
- Trap flag (TF)
- Interrupt flag (IF)
- Direction flag (DF)
- Overflow flag (OF)

5. In 8086 microcontroller, a queue is a data structure that stores data in a first-in-first-out (FIFO) order. It is implemented using the stack segment register (SS) and the stack pointer register (SP). The queue is created by initializing the SS and SP registers to a specific memory location, and data is pushed into the queue using the PUSH instruction and popped from the queue using the POP instruction.```

[17/04/23, 8:39:22â€¯AM] Prasanna Raj: 1. Knapsack Travelling: A problem in which a traveler has to pack a knapsack with a limited capacity while maximizing the value of the items packed.

2. Convex: A shape or curve that is curved outward or has no indentations.

3. Binarysort: A sorting algorithm that divides a list into two halves, sorts each half recursively, and then merges the two halves back together.

4. Quick sort: A sorting algorithm that selects a pivot element and partitions the list into two sub-lists, one containing elements smaller than the pivot and the other containing elements larger than the pivot. It then recursively sorts the two sub-lists.

5. Optimal binary search tree: A binary search tree that minimizes the expected cost of searching for a key in the tree.

6. Huffman coding: A data compression technique that assigns variable-length codes to characters based on their frequency of occurrence in the input data.

7. Assignment problem: A problem in which a set of tasks must be assigned to a set of workers, each with different capacities and costs, such that the total cost is minimized.

8. Job sequencing: A problem in which a set of jobs must be scheduled on a single machine, subject to precedence constraints and minimizing the total completion time.

[30/04/23, 12:12:00â€¯PM] Prakash: 1) The Program Status Word (PSW) contains status bits that reflect the current CPU state. The 8051 variants provide one special function register called PSW with this status information.
[30/04/23, 12:12:01â€¯PM] Prakash: 2) The data pointer or DPTR is a 16-bit register. It is made up of two 8-bit registers called DPH and DPL. Separate addresses are assigned to each of DPH and DPL. These 8-bit registers are used for the storing the memory addresses that can be used to access internal and external data/code.

32 general purpose registers each of 8-bit

Three internal and two external Interrupts
Four 8-bit ports,(short model have two 8-bit ports)
16-bit program counter and data pointer

[11/05/23, 1:32:51â€¯AM] Rajan: 1. Knapsack Travelling: A problem in which a traveler has to pack a knapsack with a limited capacity while maximizing the value of the items packed.

2. Convex: A shape or curve that is curved outward or has no indentations.

3. Binarysort: A sorting algorithm that divides a list into two halves, sorts each half recursively, and then merges the two halves back together.

4. Quick sort: A sorting algorithm that selects a pivot element and partitions the list into two sub-lists, one containing elements smaller than the pivot and the other containing elements larger than the pivot. It then recursively sorts the two sub-lists.

5. Optimal binary search tree: A binary search tree that minimizes the expected cost of searching for a key in the tree.

6. Huffman coding: A data compression technique that assigns variable-length codes to characters based on their frequency of occurrence in the input data.

7. Assignment problem: A problem in which a set of tasks must be assigned to a set of workers, each with different capacities and costs, such that the total cost is minimized.

8. Job sequencing: A problem in which a set of jobs must be scheduled on a single machine, subject to precedence constraints and minimizing the total completion time.

[20/07/23, 8:51:03â€¯AM] Praveen : 1. Define Linear Programming problem?
2. List out steps of Modelling phases?
3. Point out the properties of Linear programming solution?
4. List the four assumptions in Linear programming?
5. Describe the principal components of Decision problem?
 6.Locate suitable area for assignment problem?
 7.Define operation research?
 8. Difference between balanced & unbalanced  
    in assignment & transportation problem?
 9.what is linear programming 
  10.what are the assumptions in linear   programming
11. Write methods to find basic feasible solutions ? 
12Difference between simplex & Big M Method?13. What is feasibility region? Illustrate is it necessary that it should always be a convex set?
14. Define slack variable?
15. What are Surplus variable? And compare withÂ slackÂ variable.




1.Linear programming is a mathematical optimization technique used to find the best possible solution to a problem with linear constraints and a linear objectiveÂ function.
2.Identify decision variables.
Define the objective function.
Specify constraints.
Determine feasible region.
Consider non-negativity constraints.
Refine and adjust the model.
Test the model with known solutions.
Conduct sensitivity analysis.
DocumentÂ theÂ model.

3.Optimality: The solution is optimal, representing the best possible solution given the objective function and constraints.

Feasibility: The solution is feasible, satisfying all constraints imposedÂ byÂ theÂ problem.

4.Proportionality

Additivity

Certainty

Divisibility
5.Decision maker: The individual or entity responsible for making the decision. They are tasked with evaluating options and selecting the best course of action.

Alternatives: The different choices or options available to the decision maker. These alternatives represent different potential actions or strategies that can be taken to address the problem or achieve theÂ desiredÂ outcome
6. The suitable area for the assignment problem is in personnel management and transportation/logistics
7.Operations research (OR) optimizes decision-making using math and analytical methods, improving efficiency and performance inÂ organizations.
8.Balanced: Equal supply and demand, feasible without additional adjustments.
Unbalanced: Mismatch between supply and demand, may require modifications or constraints forÂ feasibility.
9.Linear programming is a method for optimizing a linear objective function with linear constraints.
It involves maximizing or minimizing a linear objective while satisfying a set of linearÂ constraints.
10.The assumptions in linear programming are proportionality and additivity of variables, as well as certainty of input data and divisibility of decisionÂ variables.
11.Three methods to find basic feasible solutions in linear programming:

Graphical method (for two variables): Plot feasible region, identify corner points.
Corner-point method (for more than two variables): Evaluate objective function at corner points.
Simplex method: Algorithmically pivot through corner points to reach optimalÂ solution.
12.Simplex Method: It is used to solve linear programming problems with feasible initial solutions by iteratively moving towards an optimal solution.
Big M Method: It is specifically designed to handle problems with initial infeasibility by introducing artificial variables and a penalty term (M) to convert the problem into a feasible one

Simplex Method: It assumes that the initial constraints are feasible or have a feasible basic solution to start the iteration process.
Big M Method: It can handle initial infeasibility by adding artificial variables and a large penalty term (M) to make the problem feasible. The artificial variables are later eliminated in subsequentÂ iterations.
13 . The feasibility region is the set of feasible solutions in a linear programming problem. It may or may not be a convex set, depending on the nature of the constraintsÂ involved.
14 .A slack variable is a non-negative variable used in linear programming to represent the surplus or slack in a constraint, indicating the difference between the left-hand side and right-hand side ofÂ theÂ constraint.
15. Slack variables measure underutilization in a constraint (left-hand side < right-hand side), while surplus variables measure overutilization (left-hand side > right-hand side) in linearÂ programming.

Registration Link:  https://codevita.tcsapps.com/

Find below the career highlights and Registration Steps.

Career Highlights for participating in TCS CodeVita -

1. Real-time Coding experience for starting your career.

2. MockVita to prepare you for the final contest.
3. To bridge the gap between classroom coding and real-time coding experience.
4. Global recognition for participating in an international contest.
5. Fun competition and a great addition to your resume.
6. Coding prepares you to have real-time experience in building software or starting a career with it.
7. Improves your expertise in corporate problem-solving skills.
8. This prepares you for all other National qualifier testing coding tests.

9. You can take this contest from anywhere.

10. Cash prize worth US $20,000.

Please download Microsoft Authenticator from the Play Store/App Store on your phone to start the process.
Note: Kindly make sure the registration process is either done on a PC or Laptop as the QR Code needs to be scanned via cell phone.



Follow the Registration Steps for your reference or if you have doubts during the process:

Step 1: Click on Login/Register - This is the first step for both new as well as registered users. You will find the button on the top-right of the home page.

Step 2: Click on Register - Please note that once you complete your registration process, you will be able to log into the application using the Sign In option.

Step 3: Select the Region as India

Step 4: Fill in your user details. Please fill in your First Name, Last Name, Email Id, and Username (eg - Email ID without @email can be given as username)

Step 5: Accept T&C and Consent Statement - Under the Terms and Conditions document via the hyperlink on â€˜hereâ€™ and click Accept to select the second checkbox. A QR code will be displayed in the window.

Step 6: Install Microsoft Authenticator from Play Store/App Store - Click on the "+" icon. Choose Personal account in the Add Personal account and click Scan QR code.

Step 7: Scan the QR code. Scan the QR Code which is displayed after Step 5. Please enter the One-time code which is generated in the system. Click on Submit.

Step 8: You will be redirected to the profile page to complete and save the required details.

Verify your mobile number with OTP. Fill in the other necessary information like

Academic Year of Completion
Nearest TCS Location - Chennai
Institute name
Your Reference Number

       This is a gentle reminder about TCS CodeVita Season 11 conducted by TCS. In this regard, those who have not registered yet are requested to register before the deadline. Please note that there are opportunities to grab the Pre Placement / Internship Opportunity from TCS. 

 It is mandatory for all placement registered students to register via the registration link on or before 10:00 AM â€“ 11.11.2023.


Registration Link:  https://codevita.tcsapps.com/

Find below the career highlights and Registration Steps.

Career Highlights for participating in TCS CodeVita -

1. Real-time Coding experience for starting your career.

2. MockVita to prepare you for the final contest.
3. To bridge the gap between classroom coding and real-time coding experience.
4. Global recognition for participating in an international contest.
5. Fun competition and a great addition to your resume.
6. Coding prepares you to have real-time experience in building software or starting a career with it.
7. Improves your expertise in corporate problem-solving skills.
8. This prepares you for all other National qualifier testing coding tests.

9. You can take this contest from anywhere.

10. Cash prize worth US $20,000.

Please download Microsoft Authenticator from the Play Store/App Store on your phone to start the process.
Note: Kindly make sure the registration process is either done on a PC or Laptop as the QR Code needs to be scanned via cell phone.



Follow the Registration Steps for your reference or if you have doubts during the process:

Step 1: Click on Login/Register - This is the first step for both new as well as registered users. You will find the button on the top-right of the home page.

Step 2: Click on Register - Please note that once you complete your registration process, you will be able to log into the application using the Sign In option.

Step 3: Select the Region as India

Step 4: Fill in your user details. Please fill in your First Name, Last Name, Email Id, and Username (eg - Email ID without @email can be given as username)

Step 5: Accept T&C and Consent Statement - Under the Terms and Conditions document via the hyperlink on â€˜hereâ€™ and click Accept to select the second checkbox. A QR code will be displayed in the window.

Step 6: Install Microsoft Authenticator from Play Store/App Store - Click on the "+" icon. Choose Personal account in the Add Personal account and click Scan QR code.

Step 7: Scan the QR code. Scan the QR Code which is displayed after Step 5. Please enter the One-time code which is generated in the system. Click on Submit.

Step 8: You will be redirected to the profile page to complete and save the required details.

Verify your mobile number with OTP. Fill in the other necessary information like

Academic Year of Completion
Nearest TCS Location - Chennai
Institute name
Your Reference Number

[02/12/23, 3:46:12â€¯PM] Pradeep: class DayOfWeek:
    def __init__(self, day_number):
        self.day_number = day_number

    def displayDay(self):
        days = {
            1: "Sunday",
            2: "Monday",
            3: "Tuesday",
            4: "Wednesday",
            5: "Thursday",
            6: "Friday",
            7: "Saturday"
        }
        return days.get(self.day_number, "Invalid day number")

# Get input from the user
day_number = int(input())

# Create an instance of the DayOfWeek class
day_instance = DayOfWeek(day_number)

# Display the day of the week
print(day_instance.displayDay())

[09/12/23, 7:08:02â€¯PM] Prem Kumar: #include <stdio.h>

// Function to find the sum of diagonal elements in a square matrix
int diagonal_sum(int matrix[100][100], int n) {
    // Calculate the sum of diagonal elements
    int sum = 0;
    for (int i = 0; i < n; i++) {
        sum += matrix[i][i];
    }

    return sum;
}

int main() {
    int n, m;

    // Input: Number of rows and columns
    scanf("%d %d", &n, &m);

    // Check if the matrix is square
    if (n != m) {
        printf("Not a square matrix\n");
        return 0;
    }

    int matrix[100][100];

    // Input: Elements of the matrix
    for (int i = 0; i < n; i++) {
        for (int j = 0; j < m; j++) {
            scanf("%d", &matrix[i][j]);
        }
    }

    // Output: Sum of diagonal elements
    int result = diagonal_sum(matrix, n);
    printf("%d\n", result);

    return 0;
}

[28/12/23, 12:24:44â€¯PM] Priyadarshan: Program 1:

#include <math.h>
#include <stdio.h>

const static double PI = 3.141592654;
const static double HALF_PI = PI / 2;
const static double EACH_AREA = 50;

int diffuse(double x, double y);

int main(void) {
    int testCase = 0;
    scanf("%d", &testCase);
    for (int i = 1; i <= testCase; i++) {
        double x, y;
        scanf("%lf %lf", &x, &y);
        int cnt = diffuse(x, y);
        printf("Property %d: This property will begin eroding in year %d.\n", i, cnt);
    }
    printf("END OF OUTPUT.\n");

    return 0;
}

int diffuse(double x, double y) {
    double R2 = x * x + y * y;
    double Area = HALF_PI * R2;
    return (int)ceil(Area / EACH_AREA);
}
[28/12/23, 12:25:17â€¯PM] Priyadarshan: program 2:

#include <stdio.h>
#include <stdlib.h>
#include <string.h>

int main()
{
    int t = 1;
    getchar();
    while (t--)
    {
        char s[1000];
        fgets(s, sizeof(s), stdin);
        int n = strlen(s);
        int n9 = 0;
        char res[1000] = "", num[1000] = "";
        for (int i = 0; i < n; i++)
        {
            n9 = 0;
            strcpy(num, "");
            while (s[i] >= '0' && s[i] <= '9')
            {
                if (s[i] == '9')
                    n9 = 1;
                strncat(num, &s[i], 1);
                i++;
            }
            if (!n9 && strcmp(num, "") != 0)
            {
                long long a = atoll(num);
                long long b = -1;
                if (strcmp(res, "") != 0)
                    b = atoll(res);
                if (a > b)
                    strcpy(res, num);
            }
        }
        if (strcmp(res, "") == 0)
            printf("-1");
        else
            printf("%s\n", res);
    }
    return 0;
}

[11/01/24, 9:04:44â€¯PM] Priyadarshan: from collections import defaultdict

def add_edge(graph, u, v):
    graph[u].append(v)

def dfs(graph, vertex, visited, stack):
    visited[vertex] = True
    for neighbor in graph[vertex]:
        if not visited[neighbor]:
            dfs(graph, neighbor, visited, stack)
    stack.append(vertex)

def transpose_graph(graph):
    transposed = defaultdict(list)
    for vertex in graph:
        for neighbor in graph[vertex]:
            transposed[neighbor].append(vertex)
    return transposed

def dfs_scc(graph, vertex, visited, component):
    visited[vertex] = True
    component.append(vertex)
    for neighbor in graph[vertex]:
        if not visited[neighbor]:
            dfs_scc(graph, neighbor, visited, component)

def strongly_connected_components(graph, vertices):
    stack = []
    visited = [False] * vertices

    for vertex in range(vertices):
        if not visited[vertex]:
            dfs(graph, vertex, visited, stack)

    transposed_graph = transpose_graph(graph)
    visited = [False] * vertices
    components = []

    while stack:
        vertex = stack.pop()
        if not visited[vertex]:
            component = []
            dfs_scc(transposed_graph, vertex, visited, component)
            components.append(component)

    return components

# Input
n = int(input("Enter the number of edges: "))
graph = defaultdict(list)

for _ in range(n):
    a, b = map(int, input().split())
    add_edge(graph, a, b)

# Output
components = strongly_connected_components(graph, n)
for component in components:
    print(" ".join(map(str, component)))

[26/02/24, 6:42:29â€¯AM] Sha: VC dimension: Measure of the capacity of a hypothesis class in binary classification. It represents the maximum number of points that can be shattered by the class.

Machine Learning: Field of study that gives computers the ability to learn without being explicitly programmed. It involves algorithms that improve their performance on a task as they are exposed to more data.

Occam's Razor: Principle that suggests among competing hypotheses, the one with the fewest assumptions should be selected. In machine learning, it favors simpler models over complex ones to prevent overfitting.

Types of learning: Supervised learning (with labeled data), unsupervised learning (without labeled data), and reinforcement learning (learning from feedback through interaction with an environment).

0/1 loss function: A loss function that penalizes predictions as either entirely correct (0 loss) or entirely incorrect (1 loss), without considering the degree of error.

Naive Bayes: A probabilistic classifier based on Bayes' theorem with strong independence assumptions between features. It's commonly used for text classification tasks.

Bayes theorem: A fundamental theorem in probability theory that describes the probability of an event, based on prior knowledge of conditions that might be related to the event. It's a key concept in Bayesian statistics and machine learning.

Bias and variance: Bias refers to the error introduced by approximating a real-world problem with a simplified model. Variance refers to the model's sensitivity to changes in the training data, leading to high variability in predictions. Balancing bias and variance is crucial for building accurate machine learning models

[29/02/24, 8:44:37â€¯AM] Prasanna Raj: 1. Compiler: Translates entire source code to machine code before execution.
Interpreter: Executes source code line by line, translating and executing each line in sequence.

2. Buffer pair: Two buffers used for efficient I/O operations, where one buffer is filled while the other is being read or written.

3. FIRST() and FOLLOW() functions: Functions used in parsing to determine the first set of terminals that can appear in a string derived from a grammar symbol, and the set of terminals that can immediately follow a non-terminal in any derivation.

4. Token: Smallest unit of lexical analysis, categorized by a type and a value.
Pattern: Description of the structure of a token.
Lexeme: Actual sequence of characters in the source program that matches the pattern for a token.

5. Handle: A substring of right sentential form that matches the production body in a leftmost derivation.
Handle Pruning: Elimination of intermediate steps in a leftmost derivation to reduce the number of handles.

6. Problems with top-down parsing: Left recursion, backtracking, ambiguity, and the inability to handle left-recursive grammars.

7. Conflicts in Shift Reduce Parser: Shift-reduce conflicts arise when both shifting and reducing are possible at a certain parsing state, leading to ambiguity in the parsing process.

[06/05/24, 12:10:54â€¯PM] Premachandar: The mapper's job in Hadoop is to process data. If the output directory specified in the output format already exists, MapReduce execution typically seeks further instructions, although the exact behavior can depend on the specific configuration.

Apache YARN stands for Yet Another Resource Negotiator. It's a framework-specific entity in Hadoop that negotiates resources from the Resource Manager.

Part B:

1. **Define MapReduce:**
MapReduce is a programming model and processing technique used for parallel processing of large datasets in distributed computing environments. It divides the processing into two phases: Map phase for data filtering and sorting, and Reduce phase for summarization and aggregation of the results from the Map phase.

2. **What is Data Serialization?**
Data Serialization is the process of converting structured data or object state into a format that can be easily stored, transmitted, or reconstructed later. It's commonly used in data storage, data exchange between systems, and in distributed computing to serialize objects for transmission over a network.

3. **Why use YARN in Hadoop?**
YARN (Yet Another Resource Negotiator) is used in Hadoop to manage cluster resources efficiently by separating the resource management and job scheduling functionalities from the MapReduce engine. It allows multiple data processing engines to run simultaneously on Hadoop clusters, improving resource utilization and overall performance.

4. **Differentiate between MapReduce and YARN:**
MapReduce is a programming model and processing paradigm used for distributed processing of large datasets, while YARN is a resource management framework in Hadoop that manages cluster resources and schedules jobs. YARN enables multiple processing engines to run on Hadoop clusters, not just MapReduce.

5. **List out the YARN Features:**
- Scalability: YARN can handle large-scale clusters with thousands of nodes.
- Flexibility: Supports multiple processing engines like MapReduce, Apache Spark, Apache Flink, etc.
- Resource Management: Efficiently manages cluster resources like CPU, memory, and disk.
- Fault Tolerance: Provides fault tolerance mechanisms for job execution.
- Compatibility: Integrates with various Hadoop ecosystem tools and frameworks.
- Dynamic Resource Allocation: Dynamically allocates resources based on application requirements.
- Security: Provides security features like authentication and authorization.

[06/08/24, 11:20:58â€¯AM] Prasanna Raj: FORMAT AND GUIDELINES TO PREPARE PROJECT REPORT 
The following sequence of topics to be maintained in the Project Report: Title Page
Bonafide Certificate
Bonafide from the place where the work is carried out, on their letter head
Declaration
Acknowledgement â€“ Order of names to be acknowledged (refer page no. 4 for hierarchy)
Abstract of the work Contents with page numbers List of Abbreviations, ifapplicable
List of figures, list of tables, if applicable
Chapter â€“ 1, Introduction
Chapter â€“ 2, Aim and Scope of the present investigation
Chapter â€“ 3, Experimental or materials and methods; algorithms used Chapter â€“ 4, Results and Discussion, PerformanceAnalysis
Chapter â€“ 5, Summary and Conclusions
References (in the following order only)
-	forJournals â€“nameofauthors,journalname,volumenumber,yearofpublication, page numbers - starting and ending.
-	For Books â€“ name of author, title, name of editor, publisher, year, pagenumbers.
-	Valid internetarticles.
Sub chapters should be numbered as follows:
Eg. Sub Chapter of chapter 1 should be numbered as Chapter 1.1 Further sub chapters should be numbered as 1.1.1, 1.1.2 ,â€¦.
Letter Font and Line spacings:
To be followed throughout the project work
Linespace	â€“1.5
FontSize	- 12
FontType	-Arial
Marginspace	- Left 3cm; Right â€“ 2.5cm; Top- 2.5cm; and Bottom â€“ 2.5cm

Major headings â€“ all caps â€“ 14 font size
Sub headings â€“ all caps â€“ 12 font size Further sub headings â€“ 12 font size, bold, italics Still further sub headings â€“ 12 font size, italics
Legend for Figures & tables: (Numbering should start with each chapter Number)
Figure â€“ Fig:1.1 : Self descriptive title, 12 font size, italics, bold (should be below the figure) Table â€“ Table 1.1 : self descriptive title, 12 font size, bold (should be above the table)
Note: Fig 1.1 refers to Figure 1 of chapter 1, Fig 2.2 refers to fig 2 of Chapter 2
Note : Table 1.1 refers to Table 1 of Chapter 1, Table 3.2 refers to Table 2 of Chapter 3.
Page numbers should be centered in the number format 1,2,3â€¦.. at the bottom of each page, starting from Introduction chapter onwards.
For Abstract, Contents, List of Abbreviations, List of figures, list of tables â€“ the page numbers should be in the Roman Number format (i), (ii), (iii)â€¦â€¦â€¦â€¦ and centered at the bottom of the page.

Dear Students,
       This is to inform you that all the eligible and interested students are requested to fill the form below for test location preference.



Registration:

All the eligible & interested students are requested to register in the Below two Links & Placement portal on or before 16.08.24-9.00 AM


Placement Link: https://forms.gle/zNAdSG3qCJ4Kuh4Y6

Company Link: http://nextstep.tcs.com/campus

Instructions to apply in the company link:
Â·         Students to visit http://nextstep.tcs.com/campus

Â·         Click on â€œRegister Nowâ€.

Â·         Choose the category as â€œITâ€

Â·         Fill up the details to get a Reference ID.

Â·         Proceed to complete the Application Form.

Â·         Click on â€˜Apply for Driveâ€™



If you are facing any issues in TCS registration portal, you can mail us by replying to this mail on or before registration deadline

Note: 
1. It is a must for all the students to give Chennai as the 1st option for location preference and you can give other 2nd & 3rd preferences as per your convenience. If you give any other location for 1st preference, we will change it as per the rules.
2. Students who are doing On Campus Internships in other states can give any location as per your convenience.
3. Your 3 preferences must be different from one another. If you give the same locations, we will change it as per the rules.
4. Kindly ignore the old placement registration link, you can register in the above two links. Only students who were registering in the Placement portal and above two links will be considered for this drive.
5. Your Application status must be "Applied for Drive" in the TCS portal. You can check it out in the TCS portal.
6.Students who were having old DT numbers (reference id's starting with DT-2022 or DT-2021) will not be considered. You are requested to create new Id's.

[19/08/24, 10:32:27â€¯AM] Prem: class TreeNode:
    def __init__(self, val=0, left=None, right=None):
        self.val = val
        self.left = left
        self.right = right

def kthLargest(root, k):
    # This array will store the nodes in descending order
    nodes = []

    # Helper function to perform a reverse in-order traversal
    def reverseInOrderTraversal(node):
        if node is None or len(nodes) >= k:
            return
        reverseInOrderTraversal(node.right)
        if len(nodes) < k:
            nodes.append(node.val)
        reverseInOrderTraversal(node.left)

    reverseInOrderTraversal(root)
    return nodes[-1] if len(nodes) == k else None

# Example usage:
# Constructing the BST
root = TreeNode(5)
root.left = TreeNode(3)
root.right = TreeNode(7)
root.left.left = TreeNode(2)
root.left.right = TreeNode(4)
root.right.left = TreeNode(6)
root.right.right = TreeNode(8)

k = 3  # Find the 3rd largest element
result = kthLargest(root, k)
print(result)  # Output should be 6

[22/08/24, 11:20:09â€¯AM] Sha: def friendship(N, M, A, B):
    # Union-Find Data Structure Initialization
    parent = list(range(N + 1))
    rank = [0] * (N + 1)
    
    def find(x):
        if parent[x] != x:
            parent[x] = find(parent[x])
        return parent[x]
    
    def union(x, y):
        rootX = find(x)
        rootY = find(y)
        if rootX != rootY:
            if rank[rootX] > rank[rootY]:
                parent[rootY] = rootX
            elif rank[rootX] < rank[rootY]:
                parent[rootX] = rootY
            else:
                parent[rootY] = rootX
                rank[rootX] += 1

    # Apply union operations based on the given pairs
    for i in range(M):
        union(A[i], B[i])
    
    # Calculate the size of each circle
    from collections import defaultdict
    circle_size = defaultdict(int)
    for i in range(1, N + 1):
        root = find(i)
        circle_size[root] += 1
    
    # Calculate the number of valid pairs
    sizes = list(circle_size.values())
    total_ways = 0
    total_count = sum(sizes)
    
    for size in sizes:
        total_ways += size * (total_count - size)
    
    # Each pair is counted twice (once as (i, j) and once as (j, i)), so divide by 2
    result = total_ways // 2
    
    return result

# INPUT [uncomment & modify if required]
N, M = input().split()
N = int(N)
M = int(M)
A = []
B = []
for _ in range(M):
    a, b = input().split()
    A.append(int(a))
    B.append(int(b))

# OUTPUT [uncomment & modify if required]
print(friendship(N, M, A, B))

[22/08/24, 12:59:04â€¯PM] Sha: def remove_chars(A, B):
    # Initialize an empty string for the result
    C = ''
    
    # Iterate through each character in string A
    for char in A:
        # If the character is not in string B, add it to the result
        if char not in B:
            C += char
    
    return C

# Read input strings
A = input().strip()
B = input().strip()

# Get the result and print it
print(remove_chars(A, B))
